  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d12bdea2-b211-4fb4-80a2-2f870fca515a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText6208184407848783616" style="display:none"><i>If there’s one thing Mare Barrow knows, it’s that she’s different.</i><br /><br />Mare Barrow’s blood is red—the color of common folk—but her Silver ability, the power to control lightning, has turned her into a weapon that the royal court tries to control. <br /><br />The crown calls her an impossibility, a fake, but as she makes her escape from Maven, the prince—the friend—who betrayed her, Mare uncovers something startling: she is not the only one of her kind.<br /><br />Pursued by Maven, now a vindictive king, Mare sets out to find and recruit other Red-and-Silver fighters to join in the struggle against her oppressors. <br /><br />But Mare finds herself on a deadly path, at risk of becoming exactly the kind of monster she is trying to defeat. <br /><br />Will she shatter under the weight of the lives that are the cost of rebellion? Or have treachery and betrayal hardened her forever?<br /><br />The electrifying next installment in the Red Queen series escalates the struggle between the growing rebel army and the blood-segregated world they’ve always known—and pits Mare against the darkness that has grown in her soul.</span>

        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_475').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1198150096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198150096" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198150096?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29482005-rachel-e-carter?shelf=br">br</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198150096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3180883706112370912">I am still #teamMaven. Scroll down to the spoiler portion of my review to read my theory on his redemption arc. I'm either right or dead wrong, but my gut is telling me to there is more to Maven than meets the eye.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Mare, I am very afraid for you. Things have been done to you, things no person should suffer. You've seen horrible things, done horrible things, and they will change you. I'm so afraid for what you could be, if given the wrong chance."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455038186ra/18046807.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Enter the world of shades of gray. No charact</span>
  <span id="freeText3180883706112370912" style="display:none">I am still #teamMaven. Scroll down to the spoiler portion of my review to read my theory on his redemption arc. I'm either right or dead wrong, but my gut is telling me to there is more to Maven than meets the eye.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Mare, I am very afraid for you. Things have been done to you, things no person should suffer. You've seen horrible things, done horrible things, and they will change you. I'm so afraid for what you could be, if given the wrong chance."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455038186ra/18046807.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Enter the world of shades of gray. No character will be spared.<br><br><b>I FINISHED. AND I HAVE MANY, MANY THOUGHTS.</b> Let me try to get them down coherently in GIF's (find my review of Red Queen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058639947?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>):<br><br>1. First 50% I was mostly bored. &gt;&gt;Not that the writing wasn't amazing, because it was, or because there wasn't action, because there was, but because there was little romance and no Maven and no palace and I just wasn't as entertained as the first book. But that all changed the second half when things got GOOD...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455041420ra/18047304.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2. A certain someone's death hit me harder than expected.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046727.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>&gt;&gt; I didn't like this person at all in the first book, and now I'm thinking I should read one of the novellas to get more of this character. <br><br>3. I really loved Mare in this book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046728.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>&gt;&gt;I'm sure some reviews will say she was moping and angry but honestly she was REAL. Mare struggled to make the right decisions and be who they wanted her to be and she was haunted by the events of book one. (Again, this series reminds me A LOT of Mockingjay-Katniss feels, but for me that's a wonderful thing because I loved Hunger Games and would gladly read scenes like that over and over. I got why it was so hard of her to let go of protecting Killorn and move into some sort of friendship with Cal. I liked that she didn't know how to interact with the children and people kept looking at her like she was a traitor to both Red <i>and</i> silver. I liked the way she kept the notes from Maven and the way she and Cal still mourned the boy they thought they had known.<br><br>4. The ending. OH DEAR LAWD THAT ENDING. Now that was an ending.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046729.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <blockquote> His expression is unreadable, but his meaning is clear. With one hand, he points at his feet. His fingers whiter than I remember.<br>I do as he says.<br>I kneel.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046730.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>&gt;&gt; Read below to understand my thoughts (everything is marked as a spoiler FYI):<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That ending with Maven. I sensed it coming but it was just as epic as I hoped. I felt less chemistry between Mare and Cal in this book (even though I'm #teamMaven I still loved Cal in the first) and while I could be dead wrong, here is what I think: <br><br><blockquote>Victoria is setting us up for a Warner-esque (of Tahereh Mafi's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>) love story between Mare and Maven. I know it makes no sense -he committed countless unexcusable crimes (a la Darkling and Warner)- but do we know for sure that was him? Do we really? Did we see him actually hurt anyone in this book? No. Okay, well technically, he did hurt Mare with that branding thing but.... Gah. I just feel like there is some sort of explanation. Maybe somehow it protects her? I dunno. I just know there is more to the story. And all of the BAD things that DID happen, <s>Cersei</s> -excuse me, Elara, was still alive and well. And do we know why she was in the prison? Do we really understand what was happening during that prison break out? Why was her hair graying and her appearance worn? I tell you why: because there is more to this whole "Maven is evil" business than meets the eye. I am getting very strong Juliette (of Shatter Me) vibes where Mare is going to start to understand or find out more about Maven in the next book and help him struggle to redeem himself by the end of the series. I am wishing for a HEA between M&amp;M but most likely I think she will help save him from himself and end up with Cal or alone. Maven is not pure evil and I don't think he is the villain the way we think he is. I think there are other factors at play that will be revealed -like how we thought Warner was pure evil in Shatter Me only to find his actions explained away in the sequels.</blockquote>
<br><br><i><b>"No one is born a monster." But I wish some people were. It would make it easier to hate them, to kill them, to forget their dead faces. "Even Maven."</b></i> I'm sorry but quotes like that hint at my suspicions so well. SHADES OF GRAY, PEOPLE, SHADES OF GRAY.<br><br>&gt;&gt;Now maybe you can think this is just wishful thinking. Your reaction to my prediction is probably this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046731.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And you can throw a hundred things Maven did in my face and tell me I can't explain all of that away.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046732.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There are people who read Shatter Me who refused to forgive Warner. I realize rooting for Maven is crazy to a rational eye, but in books I tend to love and sympathize with the villain and I'm sorry but reading that ending where Mare has given herself over to Maven in exchange for everyone's freedom... I just know there is so much potential there.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046733.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Maybe I'm wrong and he really is a psychopath. But I got chills with that ending and it was because of what we might see in the next book. I'm sorry but I'm just not getting an epic love story for Cal &amp; Mare, I think she is going to fall for Maven &amp; try to save him from himself in the next two books. I could be dead wrong and I realize I sound crazy, but I'm telling you, I think there is more to Maven than the villain Victoria has been leading us to believe. She's a master at twists and I am TELLING YOU that I think Maven is her trump card. I think Maven is end game for this series and I do not think he is pure evil even though we've only been offered evidence of the contrary. I'm calling it and if I'm wrong, well maybe I am, but my author instincts are telling me there is more than black and white, evil and good. This series is going to be about SHADES OF GRAY.<br><br>Final notes: <i>Why oh why did I have to wait a whole book to get two scenes with Maven?</i> I know why. Because Victoria is an evil genius and knows she is torturing us but it's exactly what we need to get amped up for the third book (there's four planned now, right?). Glass Sword did have second-book syndrome -it <i>was</i> building to future events and showing us character development and it was absolutely getting us to see how this world truly functioned, but it was truly necessary for the stage Victoria is planning to set. We all saw what she was capable in Red Queen, and I have faith the next two books will be a non-stop rollercoaster of madness now that she has given us all the building blocks and endeared us to all of the characters (I see what you did there!) so that she can let blood fly in the next. Did I love this book more than Red Queen? No. But I think Victoria did an excellent job preparing us for what's to come and building the world none of us really got to see in the first book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455037590ra/18046734.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1553299939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553299939" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553299939?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553299939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5661492548351588893"><blockquote>
  <i>And I am revealed for exactly what I am - a particularly stupid fish, moving from hook to hook, never learning my lesson.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>^This is a pretty good summary of the whole book.</b><br/><br/>I know some people will not like that I tried <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_' title='Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Glass Sword</a> after being really disappointed with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a>, but I've had a lot of luck with sequels lately. My dislike for first books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_' title='The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winner's Curse</a> turned into love for the later books in the series. So I thought I'd give Aveyard a second chance.<br/><br/>No disrespec</span>
  <span id="freeText5661492548351588893" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>And I am revealed for exactly what I am - a particularly stupid fish, moving from hook to hook, never learning my lesson.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>^This is a pretty good summary of the whole book.</b><br /><br />I know some people will not like that I tried <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_" title="Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword</a> after being really disappointed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>, but I've had a lot of luck with sequels lately. My dislike for first books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16069030.The_Winner_s_Curse__The_Winner_s_Trilogy___1_" title="The Winner's Curse (The Winner's Trilogy, #1) by Marie Rutkoski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a> turned into love for the later books in the series. So I thought I'd give Aveyard a second chance.<br /><br />No disrespect intended, but I really do struggle to understand the popularity of this series. Nothing about it is particularly good or compelling. YA fantasy is made up of lots of fluff, but even the lightest of romantic fantasies generally offer some excitement, some pull, even if the world-building is scarce and it is heavily diluted by romance.<br /><br />This sequel offers nothing like that. The prose is bland and the plot contains a lot of meandering between places and constant repetition. <b>Mare's narrative is tiresome and dull</b>, going over the same thoughts about Cal, Maven and her own specialness. Only the last few chapters contain any real action or story development - the rest of the book shows the characters going from place to place in search of those with special abilities who can help their mission.<br /><br />The author is too lazy to craft thought-provoking scenes and characters, only ever writing something or someone when it furthers Mare’s mission. Everything feels orchestrated around the super special Mare, none of the characters have their own identity or purpose, which makes it not only boring, but also turns every character into a chess piece, a stereotype, and a trope. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_" title="Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword</a> introduces many new characters and <b>not a single one of them is memorable</b>.<br /><br />And Mare alone cannot carry this story. If, perhaps, her character had been so strong and interesting that it didn't really matter about the one-dimensional other characters, then maybe this book wouldn't have been terrible. But Mare is neither a likable character, nor an anti-heroine that demands your sympathy anyway. She's an immature, often stupid, mess.<br /><br />Mare blends in with a sea of forgettable fantasy heroines. Even her flaws are not portrayed as such; her first-person narrative so self-obsessed. She's arrogant; always concerned with her own power and mission. She's selfish; often forgetting her family even exist and rarely expressing emotion befitting the situation. If you enjoy reading about super special heroines, stick with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>. If you'd rather read about a fascinating and morally questionable anti-heroine, then check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_" title="The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Young Elites</a>.<br /><br />For everything you could possibly be looking for, I can suggest a better book/series than this one. Unless you are actively seeking poor writing and boredom.<br /><br />The late dose of action couldn't save the book, nor could the ending that is more cliffhanger than resolution. It is a <b>boring, derivative fantasy</b> that only stands out from the crowded genre when it sits dazzling prettily on a bookshelf.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5661492548351588893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2177728821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177728821" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177728821?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=dumpster-fire">dumpster-fire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=literally-painful-to-read">literally-painful-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=mary-sue-i-will-kill-you">mary-sue-i-will-kill-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177728821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11638087241754369817"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566622837i/28042798._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>Rarely, (and I mean rarely) do I abhor a book to its very core. </b><br/><br/>In an effort to give some structure to <b>my upcoming rant,</b> I will limit myself to the things I disliked the most: The <b>title</b>, the <b>writing</b> and (of course) how our heroine is actually a<b> terrible, horrible person.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Title</u>
</b><br/><br/>I literally <b>
  <i>cannot</i>
</b> get over this title. So much over-the-top symbolism... but not in the way the author wanted. <br/><br/>All I took away from it was, <b>my God. How useless. </b><br/><br/><i>Anything</i> is better than a glass sword. A <u>wooden o</u></span>
  <span id="freeText11638087241754369817" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566622837i/28042798._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Rarely, (and I mean rarely) do I abhor a book to its very core. </b><br><br>In an effort to give some structure to <b>my upcoming rant,</b> I will limit myself to the things I disliked the most: The <b>title</b>, the <b>writing</b> and (of course) how our heroine is actually a<b> terrible, horrible person.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>The Title</u>
</b><br><br>I literally <b>
  <i>cannot</i>
</b> get over this title. So much over-the-top symbolism... but not in the way the author wanted. <br><br>All I took away from it was, <b>my God. How useless. </b><br><br><i>Anything</i> is better than a glass sword. A <u>wooden one</u>, a <u>plastic one</u>, heck...even a <u>french bread one</u> provides nourishment. <br><br>One swing of the <b>stupid glass thing</b> and the sword's gone and splintered itself. Then you're left stepping on glass shards for the next few weeks...<b>which is what it felt like to read this book. </b><br><br>Actually, I guess the title works. Glass swords - <b>cumbersome, annoying, useless...<i>just like Mare.</i></b><br><br><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br><br>For the life of me, I honestly can't say what this book was about. It was so <b>bland and repetitive </b> that I tuned out for great portions...yet, I don't think I missed a thing.<br><br>The author would either A) say the same thing <i>
  <b>three</b>
</i> times per <b>
  <i>sentence</i>
</b> or B) <b>copy-paste</b> the inane catchphrases (Red Dawn, Little Lightening Girl, Rise Red as the Dawn, etc). <br><br>I wanted to shake her - <b>I GET IT</b> THE DAWN IS RED AND MARE HAS LIGHTENING POWERS. And yet, in another three paragraphs, we are reminded just how red that dawn was and how Mare still had lightening powers.<br><br>The <b>sheer laziness of the writing </b> really annoyed the living daylights out of me.<br><br> Whenever things get the least bit tough, Mare<b> conveniently</b> finds just the perfect person with the exact right powers to achieve <u>(insert plot point here)</u>. Then side-character dies. <b>Rinse and Repeat.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>How our heroine is actually a<b> terrible, horrible person</b></u>
</b><br><br>We follow Mare and her rag-tag group of middle-aged superheros ran here and there as a <b>giant X-men recruitment fest.</b><br><br>She's so full of righteous anger and rebellious spirit that she never once thinks about the <b>implications and consequences</b> of her actions. <br><br>Honestly, I couldn't be the only one who noticed how there must have been <b>generations of powered Reds</b> living out their lives in secrecy. <br><br>Well, until Mare showed up and pressed them into her army...only to either A) ruin their lives or B) get them killed (depending on which was more convenient for the plot)<br><br>To top it all, she has <b>no feelings</b> towards the dying people other than an initial shock/squeal of outrage. You think I'm kidding? Even the other characters noticed it. <blockquote>
  <i>"You [Mare] feel no remorse for the dead...you can't control yourself." </i>
</blockquote> and yet, everyone in the book admires her bravery and strength. <br><br>They literally fawn over her like she's this amazing, self-sacrificing, pure-to-the-bone heroine. How (honestly, I want to know) does no one notice that all she does is A)<b> murder people</b> or B) <b>force them into her army.</b><br><br>In short, this is a half-star book. The half is because of the sheer effort it took to come up with over 400 pages starring Mare...I don't know how the author did it.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Listening to the bland monotone a la Amanda Dolan did this book no favors.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11638087241754369817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533997025?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1139397343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139397343" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139397343?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139397343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10406124866502056815"><b>Careful, there! Unavoidable spoilers from book #1.</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Attend to your own fate, Mare Barrow.”<br/>“And that is?”<br/>“To rise. And rise alone.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>As I sat wallowing in self-pity, speechless, angry at this cruel world, I had a revelation -- Victoria Aveyard enjoys being an evil mastermind. She enjoys making me laugh, fall in love with countless characters at the same time and then drown into an endless puddle of my own tears. And she does it with such glorious creativity that, even though my heart is breaking</span>
  <span id="freeText10406124866502056815" style="display:none"><b>Careful, there! Unavoidable spoilers from book #1.</b><br><br><i>
  <b>“Attend to your own fate, Mare Barrow.”<br>“And that is?”<br>“To rise. And rise alone.”</b>
</i><br><br>As I sat wallowing in self-pity, speechless, angry at this cruel world, I had a revelation -- Victoria Aveyard enjoys being an evil mastermind. She enjoys making me laugh, fall in love with countless characters at the same time and then drown into an endless puddle of my own tears. And she does it with such glorious creativity that, even though my heart is breaking into shards of glass, I cannot help but applaud her every time her writing mojo blows away my mind. She's done it twice already. First, with <i>Red Queen</i>. And now, with a sequel worthy of its predecessor -- <i>Glass Sword</i>. <br><br><i>Glass Sword</i> is unputdownable. If it weren't for Christmas chores and drooping eyes, I would've read it back to back, because from the beginning you're caught in a whirlwind of action, intrigue and betrayal and you cannot shut the damned book. The fast pace sets the tone, but some profound, haunting psychological echoes reframe a darker atmosphere. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ot9OPCcn7FI/VoFbYM6OQrI/AAAAAAAAPio/O0CiZd4dVYk/s1600/59999a269f6f85ed2de06a9125047845.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451318482i/17527569.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This sequel brings the story of <i>Red Queen</i> to a whole other level, exploiting the divide between Reds and Silvers in a realistic manner -- new allegiances are made, old enemies gamble their power, queens and kings fall to their knees and some of them kneel with bleeding hearts. The hunt for newbloods is on and Mare has to save as many as she can while trying to patch up the deep scars Maven carved into her soul. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-PUxyKAWCF48/VoFbZGYMOSI/AAAAAAAAPi8/woKI4uUwu3s/s1600/dd68f40c97e94e032032ace7328fdd83.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="314" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451319079i/17527607.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And this is where the main big difference between these installments lays. <b>Mare</b>. The time spent with the Silvers molded her into something entirely unique -- Red and Silver alike, not just her blood and abilities, but her mentality as well. Mare, at her core, remains the heroine we've been introduced to in the first book. She's strong. She's badass. She's selfish around the edges. She's brave and she's cunning. But she's shackled by guilt. She's haunted by memories. She's weaving webs of lies and she's loosing herself into an abyss of heartache and, not surprisingly, fear. Who wouldn't after such treacherous events? Not to mention her trust issues that, even if they resemble paranoia sometimes, are good reasoned. <br><br><i>
  <b>“If I am a sword, I am a sword made of glass, and I feel myself beginning to shatter.”</b>
</i><br><br>However, I adored her. I had a bit of a trouble supporting her in the prequel thanks to her double faced demeanor, but now she had my unwavering respect and admiration. I know some readers will feel conflicted about her occasional stumble into merciless, ruthless, vindictive and Silver-like behavior, but I felt it justified, although sad. And for the love of gods, she tries so hard and so much in this book to keep everyone safe, to concoct moves and countermoves, to get rid of her emotional instability, to escape Maven's shadow and to change the world a little bit. To make a difference. The little lightning girl is not so little anymore and I could not help but love her, because even though she loses a lot of fights with inner and outer demons, Mare always had the courage to battle for her beliefs. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-51gDVY5ZN2U/VoFbYLuu-3I/AAAAAAAAPiw/VMiNtXRWwbI/s1600/bf9ed72852a3b1cc4732721cd02f6aef.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451318320i/17527561.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I see you as you could become, no longer the lightning, but the storm. The storm that will swallow the world entire.”</b>
</i><br><br>Cal is also a great difference. He reminded me of Celaena in so many ways. Gone is the prince in his overwhelming intensity; a boy with nightmares, a thirst for revenge and endless loneliness remains. I think he's even more lost than Mare is, because his home, his people, his whole goddamn country want him dead and he's running away from people he used to care deeply for. That kind of messes with his head and it triggers subtle changes in his personality and behavior, but still -- <b>I. Loved. Him. To. Bits.</b> He's tough. Loyal. Kickass. And quite swoony -- a scene with him and a child had me dying of FEELS. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-i3Iuhxm6Noc/VoFiqbThjxI/AAAAAAAAPkY/GQBMWjmA4Ps/s1600/tumblr_michtlWLIs1qk0s41o1_250.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I made mistakes because of him. And,” he adds quietly, “I made mistakes because of you.”</b>
</i><br><br>Now on to the most interesting character of them all -- Maven. He was exactly like The Darkling in <i>Siege &amp; Storm</i> -- not there but for a few sparse pages, but always <i>there</i>. You get it or I'm talking nonsense? His presence was almost palpable for he is constant in our main characters' thoughts and whenever he does make an appearance, he only instates his wicked, power-hungry, cruel ways, making it even harder for the rest to escape his mental grasp. He's strong, cold and calculated and a wonderfully nuanced complex villain -- I'm anxious and enthusiastic at the same time for what it's to come. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4QYqwMbZKf0/VoFbYFXh1QI/AAAAAAAAPis/67Sj3gDN_aI/s1600/abae54b96484f8144728ad044c8e7891.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451318320i/17527562.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“No heart can ever be truly understood. Not even your own.”</b>
</i><br><br>I have to warn you beforehand -- the romance is certainly not the focus. Actually, I could say that it barely survived the aftermath of book 1. You can wave the fragile "love triangle" goodbye. With Maven not being physically present for most of the story, that leaves us with Mare and Cal and, um, well, to say that their relationship is complicated would be the understatement of the year. Each of them got burned by the other and they have walls in place to maintain distance. Arghh, and there's tension. And wildness. And desire. Regrets upon regrets. They still use and hurt each other. But, paradoxically, they protect one another despite their past. AND I JUST LOVED THAT. It's no secret I shipped Mare and Cal to the moon and back, so I'll admit I devoured every scene with these two in it, especially those where they just crumble without the other nearby. <i>*happy sigh*</i> <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-10J_nKxucC0/VoFbYuqUvLI/AAAAAAAAPi0/wk5s2OZzFbw/s1600/c851de1825aeb2a2d6c56024c56adb61.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="213" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451318320i/17527563.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I must keep my eyes ahead, and away from the fire of a fallen prince. I must freeze my heart to the one person who insists on setting it ablaze.”</b>
</i><br><br>To Maven's fans -- don't worry, Mare still clings to him no matter how much she tells herself not to. So you see, we have a confusing, effed up mess, one deliciously agonizing. <br><br>Let’s get to what is also known as my new favorite secondary characters. Shade and Kilorn. And even Farley. THEY WERE ASDFGHJKL. Shade especially. I completely fell in love with Shade -- he was a great addition to the cast. He's clever, easy going and just cute, not to mention that his love for his sister was awww worthy. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ksRzUtjCssU/VoFfJdJLI_I/AAAAAAAAPjo/an_ssGZlKCc/s1600/8365595.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527710.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Kilorn evolved quite much. I mean, I don't hate him anymore. I love him now. He's a central piece to the story and despite his "uselessness" he proves to be a good friend, a brave soldier and an all-around great guy. His friendship with Mare was awesome and my heart ached for his unreturned romantic feelings -- I might bless a possible Kilorn and Mare couple. I <i>might</i>. <br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-envfpd5uqW0/VoFfNrAxDFI/AAAAAAAAPkM/4ybMhHG8_rg/s1600/tumblr_inline_mp9wiz18i81qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="155" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527711.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And Farley was another kickass chick I was glad we spent more time with. She's just, courageous and determined. Plus, her fate brings a bittersweet smile on my face whenever I think about it (you can't bribe me to spill the beans). <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-vM34HUBZtnA/VoFfMdmKzvI/AAAAAAAAPkA/hgSLdOH0drw/s1600/tumblr_mtp1qpJ86y1sc9n4yo1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="189" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527712.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I have to admit there were a few flaws (but not major enough to deflect my boundless love for this book). The newbloods plotline develops and tons of characters are introduced, some of them memorable and some of them not. The world-building is not extraordinary, although we get to venture in new cities (not that it ever was in RQ) and the Red Guard only has a minor role in current events, keeping its enigmatic traits. <br><br>The mild reminiscences of <i>Shatter Me</i> linger, but this time they are coupled with <i>Breaking Dawn</i> and <i>The Young Elites</i> deja-vus due to the expansion of the newbloods' power palette. Nonetheless, there are some characters that have managed to amaze me with their original abilities and I had an overall sense of badassery every time their lot became the focus. I do have one slight regret though -- I would have liked to know each one better, because there was a gold mine of awesomeness for side stories. <br><br>Expect twists and turns. The jaw-dropping kind. The clever ones. The shit-God-no-I-wanna-go-back kind and also the yeah-you-are-going-down-bitches kind. These twists are part of what makes GS a thrilling sequel -- no one is safe, no newblood, no Red and, for once, no Silver. And <b>I CRIED A LOT THANKS TO THESE TWISTS.</b><br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cK3iuZFWC4k/VoFfLtKwCAI/AAAAAAAAPj8/nVkvR-3OqPI/s1600/tumblr_mklluuLPeG1s9ft09o1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="134" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527713.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But <b>HOLY GODS THAT FREAKING ENDING</b>. I had tears streaming down my face because I thought the book will most likely end on a sorrowful note, you know, I expected that, but then shit just hit the fan, K-BOOM, pow-pow, things I didn't expect happened in a matter of a few lines and I was left crumbling on a cliffhanger that gutted me. Nooo, the author just couldn't have kept me sane and I AM HERE WONDERING HOW TO FAST-FORWARD MY LIFE TO GET MY HANDS ON THE NEXT BOOK, because while the last few pages killed me, the epilogue pretty much stomped on my grave. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Love blinds.”</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oFgMCakJfCY/VoFfIxmXBxI/AAAAAAAAPjk/SKMt14700NM/s1600/tumblr_inline_mmazychFWT1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="133" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451320005ra/17527714.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The decision to expand this series into a four-volume saga couldn't have been more right, because there's no way in hell Aveyard could tie up all the loose ends we're left with in just one novel. And even if she would, there are worlds to be explored. Kings to be conquered. Queens to be made. And you don't want that exquisite potential to feel rushed. Regardless, I have a feeling the dynamic will change dramatically in the third book. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-TRercpCjLZ8/VoFbZVwZn5I/AAAAAAAAPjA/Q4u0O0rQbH4/s1600/e60fe43a491e4e4779b55ef6ac2a86bf.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="179" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451318320i/17527564.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I am a weapon made of flesh, a sword covered in skin.”</b>
</i><br><br><i>Glass Sword</i> was an electrifying sequel (shhh, let my pun be). It was an emotional roller coaster, one careening towards an explosive final, riveting, surprising, vivid and glorious. It made me cry, smile in anticipation and crave more and more of this enthralling universe. <i>Glass Sword</i> is exactly what a sequel should be and I cannot wait to see what the dawn brings for these amazing characters. <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3</b><br><br>P.S. This review contains quotes subject to change. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10406124866502056815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266517140" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266517140?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=longer-than-necessary">longer-than-necessary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=slow">slow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266517140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8580550498350363889"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455640475ra/18130245.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Basically <i>Mockingjay</i></b><br/><br/>After I finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257295638?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Red Queen</i>
</a>, I suspected there would be a large problem with the sequel: too many characters and details. I was correct that I wouldn't remember them because the author just launches into the story here without as much as a <i>previously on</i> to refresh the audience with the story and cast. This works against the story from the very beginning, because unless the reader just finished the first book, it's all a very confusing game of catch up.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456764119ra/18274368.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Adding to that confus</span>
  <span id="freeText8580550498350363889" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455640475ra/18130245.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Basically <i>Mockingjay</i></b><br><br>After I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257295638?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Red Queen</i>
</a>, I suspected there would be a large problem with the sequel: too many characters and details. I was correct that I wouldn't remember them because the author just launches into the story here without as much as a <i>previously on</i> to refresh the audience with the story and cast. This works against the story from the very beginning, because unless the reader just finished the first book, it's all a very confusing game of catch up.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456764119ra/18274368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Adding to that confusion is a weird round of c/k name games. Kilorn, Cal, Cameron, Corros, Corvium, Ketha... I mean, the author's head is obsessed with these sounds and it does the reader no favors in distinguishing these characters and places from one another.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452030970ra/17636998.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To further confuse you, Aveyard spends the first half of the book in action sequences that are also pretty chaotic and don't do much for the story. I get that the author is a screenwriter and these scenes probably would look great on film but she needs to learn to write them for readers instead of directors. As if sensing that the first half is all action, she overcorrects and spends most of the rest of the book with exposition. It doesn't balance out the book; it makes it a slog to read as info dump after info dump weight down the already-too-thin story. Seriously, there's maybe only 80 pages of storyline here stretched into 440+ pages. <br><br>As others have already said, this series gets less and less original as it goes on. <i>Glass Sword</i> borrows heavily from the disappointing finale to the <i>Hunger Games</i> series. I know: Looking for originality in YA these days is fruitless, but one can hope, can't they? And the villain, Maven, is basically Joffrey Baratheon.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456764800ra/18274439.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And Shade, the teleporter basically gets the Dobby treatment.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456765321ra/18274539.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Look, I love the cover of this book and the first one, but there doesn't seem more to this series other than a pretty face anymore. I'm sorry, but Aveyard is going to squeeze this thing into at least 2 more books but I doubt there is any juice left. So I give up on this once-promising series.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438379122ra/15700544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8580550498350363889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1220365494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220365494" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1220365494?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1220365494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3876373553826826661"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If I am a sword, I am a sword made of glass, and I feel myself beginning to shatter.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>I would be more than willing to be the one who shatters you and stomps on your pieces, insufferable lightning girl!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463931901ra/19176616.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I swear I have no idea how I managed to finish <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_' title='Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Glass Sword</a>. I'm not saying this because I found the plot slow like I read on many reviews, or because it suffered from second-book-syndrome, but because <b>for the first time in my life I wanted to physically hurt the heroine with such a see</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3876373553826826661" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If I am a sword, I am a sword made of glass, and I feel myself beginning to shatter.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>I would be more than willing to be the one who shatters you and stomps on your pieces, insufferable lightning girl!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463931901ra/19176616.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I swear I have no idea how I managed to finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_" title="Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword</a>. I'm not saying this because I found the plot slow like I read on many reviews, or because it suffered from second-book-syndrome, but because <b>for the first time in my life I wanted to physically hurt the heroine with such a seething passion. </b>It's like Mare's face was calling for my fist.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451353378ra/17531544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Mare is a horrible, <b><i>horrible</i></b> person.</u><br><br>I gave up every effort to understand her and instead I started imagining which death is more appropriate for her. <b>She kept acting like a martyr and God's greatest creation and gift to all those unfortunate souls who were not powerful and amazing like her.</b> Hey your Superiorness, I have news for you! Power doesn't come from the random ability to manipulate the elements around you, power can be found in sharp minds and kind hearts. Your lack of brain and heart makes you a weak and pathetic brat that only cares about herself and the other newbloods and ignores everyone else. There was actually a point where she wondered how Kilorn managed to survive since he was no one, just a simple fisher boy! I am not a fan of Kilorn (I found him annoying most of the times but he surprisingly grew on me towards the end) but I wanted to cut my arm and throw it at her! Always thinking her decisions are the best, always ignoring the voice of reason, always so <b>self-righteous</b> and <b>self-involved</b>, eager to manipulate and control, to sacrifice others for her own purposes. The way she kept judging and blaming Cal made my blood boil. She accused him of fearing to act when he wanted to show mercy, a concept unknown to her, she judged him for not trying to make things better for the poor when she was the one who stole from the poor to satisfy her selfish needs, and I keep wondering how did she know that he wouldn't change things when he never had the chance. <i>She</i> turned his world upside down, <i>she</i> betrayed him and took everything from him, <b><i>she</i> was his downfall</b>.<br><b>I hate her.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Kneel or bleed.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And <b>I also hate Maven</b>. I can't find any redeeming quality in him, I knew from the very start how rotten and corrupted he was. He's not a misguided soul that started off as good and lost his way, he didn't exprerience an upleasant childhood or a trauma that made him this monster, he is just <b>evil</b>. He craves power, he's full of jealousy and hatred, <b>he.murdered.<i>babies</i>.</b> for heaven's sake to make a point! But I can't help but admit he's one of the reasons that made this book so <b>gripping</b>, while he had very few scenes, he was always present, making you shiver.<br><blockquote>
  <b><i>“I am your rightful king, Silver-born for centuries. The only reason </i>you're<i> still breathing is because I can't burn the oxygen from this room.” </i></b>
</blockquote><br><b>I love Cal.</b> He's the victim of the worst betrayal, he has no one, he is no one, he clings to Mare and tries to salvage the humanity that's left in her but he rarely succeeds. He doesn't belong anywhere, he's broken and scarred but he's still noble, he endures the mistrust and the insults and he starts to realize the awfully wrong way the world works. He is smart and kind and by far <b>the best character</b> in this book. I just want to hug him and tell him everything's going to be alright.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463936619ra/19177060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for the plot, I loved the idea of recruiting newbloods, it <b>reminded me of Professor X and Magneto in X-Men First Class</b> (only <i>they</i> did not force anyone to join them) and <b>Hunger Games</b> at the same time, with the revolution brewing. There were times I wished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7074943.Victoria_Aveyard" title="Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Aveyard</a> didn't elaborate so much in some scenes, but in general I found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_" title="Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword</a> <b>action-packed</b> and I was constantly afraid of what was about to happen next, I was fully invested to the story with its schemes and beautifully crafted fight scenes and plot-twists! And of course, the world-building was utterly intriguing, the <b>blend of modern technology and dystopia and high fantasy</b> is what won me over in the first place!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I am a weapon made of flesh, a sword covered in skin. I was born to kill a king, to end a reign of terror before it can truly begin.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>(well <i>you</i> gave this reign of terror the chance to begin but there's no point repeating that, right?)<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7074943.Victoria_Aveyard" title="Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Aveyard</a> is without a doubt a <b>very talented author</b>, and the fact that she created so many flawed and three dimensional characters and inflicted so many emotions (albeit the most dominant ones were wrath and terror) is proof enough! The <b>cliffhanger</b> though shattered any resolve I had left, which means<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463936619ra/19177061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I need some anger management sessions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3876373553826826661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1199873793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199873793" />
    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35007929-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415626292p2/35007929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1199873793?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/35007929-cody">Cody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=to-be-released">to-be-released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35007929-cody?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1199873793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1505396870016360295">Glass Sword picks up straight after the explosive ending of Red Queen. Mare and Cal are now with the Scarlet Guard but that doesn’t mean they’re safe, far from it. They're being hunted down by Maven, who is now the King of Norta. The race is on to find these so-called ‘New Bloods’: Reds who possess the powers of Slivers, the only question is, who will get to them first; Mare or Maven?<br/><br/> It’s really hard to talk about Glass Sword without giving away spoilers but anyway the whole point of the book i</span>
  <span id="freeText1505396870016360295" style="display:none">Glass Sword picks up straight after the explosive ending of Red Queen. Mare and Cal are now with the Scarlet Guard but that doesn’t mean they’re safe, far from it. They're being hunted down by Maven, who is now the King of Norta. The race is on to find these so-called ‘New Bloods’: Reds who possess the powers of Slivers, the only question is, who will get to them first; Mare or Maven?<br><br> It’s really hard to talk about Glass Sword without giving away spoilers but anyway the whole point of the book is to track down these New Bloods, King Maven will obviously send them to their death as they undermine his rule, after all Mare was portrayed to be Mareena Titanos, a lost Sliver girl living with Reds. Mare wants to find the new bloods to protect them from Maven’s wrath, she gives them a choice, runaway or join The Scarlet Guard who's mission is to dethrone the sadistic King. So it’s basically a wild goose chase for Mare, she must find the New Bloods before Maven, protect her family, as well as avoiding capture because she’s now a traitor to the crown.<br><br>Mare changes a lot in this book and not all of it was for the better, she was cunning, ruthless and sometimes cruel. I actually expected this change, in order for Mare to go up against Maven and his mother she needed to evolve and look at her past mistakes. However, Mare became my biggest problem, she lost the fire she had in Red Queen and instead became this husk of herself. I think she also suffered from a huge case of delusions of grandeur; her powers became somewhat god-like in Glass Sword and instead of giving of the impression of ‘Mare, Queen of Reds’, there was a lot of cringing and eye-rolling and <b>just get on with it</b> moments!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454795806ra/18015563.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So, I think everyone knew my opinions on the romance of RQ and I can happily say this love-square is over! There are no new love interests for Mare, thank god but the romance for Glass Sword is pretty much a giant question mark, it changes depending on Mare’s moods, I’d like to think I know what’s going to happen but honestly Glass Swords feels like a completely different book at this point, so anything is possible…. I guess.<br><br>There was a lot of adventure in this book, I loved being able to explore Norta more and in addition to adventure we got heaps of action. Speaking of action, can I just take a moment to fully appreciate our exiled Price of fire, Cal? WHOA, my only complaint is I <s>wanted</s>, <b>needed</b> more of him and if I’m honest, a lot less Mare ha! Okay, not my only complaint, basically my biggest one is with a certain action scene, basically someone died but it wasn’t explained <b>at all</b>. The whole chapter was a mess and wasn't until the next chapter that you realise 'said character' died? Huh! *sigh*<br><br>Overall Glass Sword is somewhere between a 3-4 star read, it just wasn’t able to grip me in the way RQ did and sometimes it was a struggle to carry on reading. The cliffhanger was so shocking, heartbreaking and fantastic but it didn’t really make up for everything else. As much as I would like to blame the hype with this one, I really must blame myself, I was expecting A LOT more, Glass Sword is a good book but in order to follow Red Queen, I think it needed to be a great book and sadly it just wasn’t.<br><br><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed (Blog)</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/CodyLeighDuffy" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/codyleighduffy/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> <br><br><i>Updates, before reading</i><br><b>COVER REVEAL: GLASS SWORD</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436277966i/15441253._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I LOVE IT!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388707991ra/7906243.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>TITLE REVEAL: GLASS SWORD</b><br><br>Please tell me I'm not the only one still rooting for Cal &amp; Mare? <b>TEAM CAL!</b><br><br>Also the home of <b>Team Anti-Kilorn!</b> hahaha.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434832246ra/15268571.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1505396870016360295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312156006?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books">Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312156006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5448332444567855116"><br/>This review can also be found <a href='http://wp.me/p6sNGI-8I' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>on my blog, Dana and the Books</a>.<br/><br/>Rating: 4.5/5<br/><br/>Holy hell, that ending. That last chapter. That last sentence.<br/><br/><i>Glass Sword</i> was one of my most anticipated 2016 reads and it completely lived up to the hype, making it a fantastic sequel to <i>Red Queen</i>.<br/><br/>Without giving away spoilers, <i>Glass Sword</i> started right in the action, basically right where <i>Red Queen</i> left off. The main focus of Glass Sword is to search for and recruit others like Mare Barrow for the uprising against Silver </span>
  <span id="freeText5448332444567855116" style="display:none"><br />This review can also be found <a href="http://wp.me/p6sNGI-8I" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog, Dana and the Books</a>.<br /><br />Rating: 4.5/5<br /><br />Holy hell, that ending. That last chapter. That last sentence.<br /><br /><i>Glass Sword</i> was one of my most anticipated 2016 reads and it completely lived up to the hype, making it a fantastic sequel to <i>Red Queen</i>.<br /><br />Without giving away spoilers, <i>Glass Sword</i> started right in the action, basically right where <i>Red Queen</i> left off. The main focus of Glass Sword is to search for and recruit others like Mare Barrow for the uprising against Silver Royalty.<br /><br />After reading <i>Red Queen</i> almost a year ago, I impatiently awaited the sequel, but I was also apprehensive. Would it live up to the first book? It most certainly did! The entire story was like watching an action movie. No boring lulls in the middle of the story, no dull scenes slowing the narrative down.<br /><br />Mare develops as a character—she becomes harder, colder, and it’s completely understandable and justifiable. Ironically, I like her because I don’t like her as a person. She makes mistakes, she makes bad decisions, and she’s selfish. It was wonderful to see her change from a scared and unconfident girl in Red Queen to a bold and powerful woman in Glass Sword.<br /><br />My only criticism is at around the halfway point, we saw a whole group of new characters introduced in the span of just a few chapters, which made it a bit difficult to remember who is who and who has what powers.<br /><br /><i>Glass Sword</i> ended on such a high note. I think Victoria Aveyard is becoming the queen of plot twists! The set up for the next book looks ridiculously exciting.<br /><br />Thanks to Orion Publishing Group for providing me with an ARC of <i>Glass Sword</i> from NetGalley!</span>

<div id="review_1282642896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282642896" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1282642896?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282642896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12987721535570892833">It's actually more of a 3.5. I just can't make up my mind about how I feel.<br/><br/>Warning: review must be read till the ending to understand the stars...........<br/><br/>I'm not sure what made me feel negative towards this book from the beginning. I guess you really shouldn't read the reviews for a book before you've read it yourself, especially if you're planning on reading the book either way. Since I opened the first page I had a sense of distaste towards it, that continued until page 200 or so. To be very h</span>
  <span id="freeText12987721535570892833" style="display:none">It's actually more of a 3.5. I just can't make up my mind about how I feel.<br /><br />Warning: review must be read till the ending to understand the stars...........<br /><br />I'm not sure what made me feel negative towards this book from the beginning. I guess you really shouldn't read the reviews for a book before you've read it yourself, especially if you're planning on reading the book either way. Since I opened the first page I had a sense of distaste towards it, that continued until page 200 or so. To be very honest my bias wasn't entirely unjustified. The first half was bad, and I don't mean to be crude, but it just wasn't entertaining or even truly bearable. Maybe it was the fact that I loved red queen so much, so the disappointment hit me harder than it should have. <br /><br />The first and biggest flaw was the dramatic monologues. The way mare kept overestimating and underestimating herself at the same time. Yes I know monologues are a vital part of characters and their personalities, but I found them more annoying than anything. It wasn't just the self pity, it was like she couldn't decide who she is. A self centered egotistical killer, a breakable weapon, or smitten heartbroken puppy. Honestly thats how it went, from conflict to confused to self assured to messy goo and the cycle would start again. So mare annoyed the living crap out of me for about 200 pages to be exact. Then there was a turn of events.<br />The pace started to pick up, and the storyline started to change all together. It went from the repetitive revolution theme to something more creative and interesting. Honestly I thought this would be like MOKINGJAY, a book which I was also terribly disappointed with. Simply because nothing happens until the last 20 pages or so. Then everything in the span of the next 10 years, revolting included occurs in the last few chapters. But thankfully it wasn't the case here. Things began to pick up pace then got better and better. I think it was mostly that the book stopped revolving around mare entirely. And towards the end I was reminded why I loved red queen so damn much.<br /><br />The ending was the worlds most dramatic cliff hanger. And shade was probably my most adored character, so I'll probably be in this emotional wreckage for the next few days. I'm so incredibly sorry that such a wonderful ending had to be tainted by that beginning. <br />But I think the struggle of the begging was worth it once I got to the second half. It was truly an excellent second half. So the stars are purely for the second half, the first half is a zero from me. <br />There's no doubt that Victoria Aveyard is a talented author, albeit an inconsistent one. The story telling and characterization of red queen are proof of this. So I'll give the next book the benefit of the doubt.<br /><br />Let's see how the third book will make me feel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12987721535570892833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
